**Access Audit Checklist**

This Access Audit Checklist has been developed for use by graduates of the Access Auditing courses presented by **Access Institute.** It is copyright © and is not intended or available for circulation, reproduction or use by other parties without the written permission of Access Institute.

Where necessary it is recommended that further advice is sought from a **Qualified and Accredited Access Consultant** in order to ensure a building can fully comply with all relevant, detailed access requirements. Access Institute recommends that this advice is sought prior to access improvement works being undertaken on any building. 

**Disclaimer**  
Whilst every effort has been made by Access Institute (RTO 22404\) to ensure the accuracy, currency and reliability of the information contained in this checklist/report template, no responsibility or liability is accepted by Access Institute for any errors, omissions or inaccuracies. Users are advised to verify all information independently and apply their own professional judgement when relying on the content for decision-making or compliance purposes. Access Institute expressly disclaims any liability for loss, damage or consequence arising from reliance on this material.

The information in this Checklist is based on the requirements of the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010, Compilation 3* and relevant Australian Standards referenced by the Premises Standards.

Elements that are necessary for compliance with the Premises Standards are identified as ‘mandatory’. These is in non-italic font. 

*Additional information and recommendations over and above these ‘*mandatory’ *requirements are identified as ‘preferred’ and are in italic font.*

# **1.0	Accessible Car Parking** {#1.0-accessible-car-parking}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for** 

			**access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**AS 2890.5 \- 1993		Parking facilities \- On Street Car Parking**

**AS / NZS 2890.6- 2009	Off street parking for people with disabilities**

**Other Relevant References**

RAA Design Guidelines for accessible Electric Vehicle Charging Stations

**Provision of parking bays for people with disabilities**

| Class of building to which the Class 7a building or car parking area is associated | Number of accessible car parking spaces required |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Class 1b and 3 (boarding / guest house, residential (see below))** |  |
| Boarding house, guest house, hostel, lodging house, backpackers accommodation, or the residential part of a hotel or motel. | To be calculated by multiplying the total number of car parking spaces by the percentage of: accessible sole occupancy units to the total number of sole occupancy units; or accessible bedrooms to the total number of bedrooms; and the calculated number is to be taken to the next whole figure. |
| Residential part of a school, accommodation for the aged, disabled or children, residential part of a health care building which accommodates members of staff or the residential part of a detention centre. | 1 space for every 100 car parking spaces or part thereof. |
| **Class 5, 7, 8 and 9c (office, car park / storage, lab / assembly, aged care)** | 1 space for every 100 car parking spaces or part thereof. |

| Class 6 (shop) |  |  |
| ----- | :---- | :---- |
| up to 1000 car parking spaces; and | 1 space for every 50 car parking spaces or part thereof. |  |
| for each additional 100 car parking spaces or part thereof in excess of 1000 car parking spaces. | 1 space. |  |
| **Class 9a (health care)** |  |  |
| Hospital (non-outpatient area) | 1 space for every 100 car parking spaces or part thereof. |  |
| Hospital (outpatient area): 	Up to 100 car parking spaces; and 	For each additional 100 car parking spaces or part thereof in excel of 1000 car parking spaces. |  |  1 space for every 50 car parking spaces or part thereof. 1 space.  |
| Nursing home |  | 1 space for every 100 car parking spaces or part thereof. |
| Clinic or day surgery not forming part of a hospital |  | 1 space for every 50 car parking spaces or part thereof. |
| **Class 9b (assembly – civic, recreation, education, entertainment)** |  |  |
| School |  | 1 space for every 100 car parking spaces or part thereof. |
| Other assembly buildings: 	up to 1000 car parking spaces; and 	for each additional 100 car parking spaces or part thereof in excess of 1000 car parking spaces. |  |  1 space for every 50 car parking spaces or part thereof. 1 space. |
| **Source: *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010*** |  |  |

**Key Access Features:**

People with disabilities will require appropriate numbers of accessible parking bays. These should be located as close as possible to the principal pedestrian entrance of the building with a continuous accessible path of travel from the parking area.

A bay is required to provide appropriate access for both the driver and passenger to load and unload mobility aids including wheelchairs and scooters, without putting users at risk of being injured by passing traffic. A user will often need to open the vehicle door fully to gain access to the vehicle. Some users may need access to a storage device on top of their vehicle so overhead clearance for ease of access is also important.

Other key access elements include provision of a level ground surface, appropriate signage and line marking, kerb ramps, lighting, overhead clearance, accessible type and location of parking payment mechanisms and tactile ground surface indicators as per relevant Australian Standards. Shelter where it can be provided assists all users in hot or wet conditions.

Signage located at the entrance to any car park in addition to the time limit and number of accessible spaces available assists users.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

* numbers of accessible parking bays are determined by the class and use of the building that they are provided for;  
* a level, firm ground surface is required;  
* vertical clearances of 2200mm are required to the designated accessible parking bay, with 2500mm required above the bay proper;  
* delineation of the accessible parking bay and shared area (angled bay) is to be with yellow lines and the dedicated space is to be provided with the international symbol of access with dimensions as set out in Australian Standards.

An angled parking bay specifically for use by people with disabilities. It is required to have:

* a dedicated space a width of 2400mm;  
* length 5400mm; and   
* with an adjoining shared pathway (at grade) a minimum width of 2400mm and length of 5400mm at the side; and   
* 2400mm long x 2400mm wide shared area at one end of the dedicated space i.e. entirely at the front or entirely at the rear of the dedicated space.

If a parallel bay is provided, it is required to have: 

* a dedicated space a minimum width of 3200mm;   
* length of 7800mm; and  
* with an adjoining shared 1600mm wide path of travel at the non-trafficable side. 

Access to the adjacent pathway shall be level or via a kerb ramp at the front or rear of the bay. 

Refer to AS 2890.5 for requirements for on-street parking for people with disabilities.

Existing accessible parking bays (within a car park associated with a building) are required to be upgraded to meet the requirements of AS 2890.6-2009 when a building changes use or the car park area is part of construction works subject to a building approval. 

**Checklist**

| 1 | Accessible Car Parking      (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1.1 | Are there appropriate numbers of designated accessible parking bays for people with disabilities provided (Note: not required to be designated if 5 or less under APS)  **APS table D3.5, DP8** |  |  |  |
| 1.2 | Do the designated accessible bay/s (DAPB) have min. overhead clearance of 2500mm  **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.4** |   |  |  |
| 1.3 | Is there an overhead clearance a min. of 2200mm at the car park entry **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.4** |  |  |  |
| 1.4 | *Is the DAPB clearly visible with elevated signs with blue international access symbol **AS / NZS 2890.6 – A3*** |  |  |  |
| 1.5 | Is the DAPB noted on the ground with the international symbol of access (white symbol between 800 – 1000mm high within a blue rectangle not more than1200 x 1200mm) located in the centre of the space between 500 – 600mm from the entry point **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 3.1** |  |  |  |
| 1.6 | Is the DAPB (dedicated) space delineated by yellow slip resistant lines (unbroken 80 – 100mm wide all sides – except any side delineated by a kerb, barrier, wall) **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 3.2** |  |  |  |
| 1.7 | Is any walkway within or partly within a shared area marked with yellow slip resistant lines (unbroken longitudinal lines on both sides – excepting any side delineated by a kerb, barrier, wall) **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 3.2** |  |  |  |
| 1.8 | **If** the DAPB is parallel (to the roadway / parking aisle), is it a min. width of 3200mm and 7800mm long with an appropriate 1600mm wide x 7800mm long connecting pathway (pathway can be above grade of bay)   **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.2.2** |  |  |  |
| 1.9 | **If** the DAPB is angled (to the roadway / parking aisle), is it 2400mm wide and 5400mm long, with an adjoining shared pathway a min of 2400mm wide x 5400 (plus 2400 x 2400 at front or rear) (must be at grade of parking bay). Is the shared area marked with diagonal stripes 150 to 200 mm wide with spaces 200 mm to 300 mm between stripes.  The stripes shall be at an angle of 45 ±10 degrees to the side of the space. **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.2.1, Cl.3.2 b) 11\)** |  |  |  |
| 1.10 | Is a bollard provided within the shared area (central in space – set back from the end of the parking module 750 – 850mm) **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.2.1(e)** |  |  |  |
| 1.11 | Is the DAPB on level ground, with a firm surface and free of loose material. Crossfall (not more 1:40 in any direction or 1:33 if bitumen / outside) **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.3** |  |  |  |

| 1 | Accessible Car Parking      (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1.12 | **If** kerbs exist, at a parallel parking bay, is there an appropriate kerb ramp (at front or rear end) provided from the DAPB (Note: pathway may require an increase in width to accommodate kerb ramp) **AS / NZS 2890.6 Cl. 2.2.2 / 2.5** |  |  |  |
| 1.13 | Do existing kerb ramp/s at parking bay, have a slip resistant surface **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1 and 7.7.3** |  |  |  |
| 1.14 | Are the existing kerb ramp/s at DAPB, a max. length of 1520mm and maximum rise of 190mm with a slope / gradient where the ratio is not greater than 1:8  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.2.2** |  |  |  |
| 1.15 | Do existing kerb ramp/s at DAPB, have a min. width of 1000mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.7** |  |  |  |
| 1.16 | Do existing kerb ramp/s have an appropriate landing at the top and bottom of the ramp (Note: consider change of direction) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.7** |  |  |  |
| 1.17 | Do the existing kerb ramp/s at DAPB, have a smooth transition between the road and pathway (max. diff. 5mm with rounded edge)   **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7** |  |  |  |
| 1.18 | Are there appropriate hazard tactile ground surface indicators (TGSIs) prior to a hazard (e.g. roadway) i.e. (600 – 800mm x path width). (Note: exceptions in A.S.) **AS 1428.4.1 Cl. 2.5** |  |  |  |
| 1.19 | *Are the DAPBs adjacent to, or as near as possible, to the principal pedestrian entry of the building or facility* |  |  |  |
| 1.20 | *Is the area for the DAPBs etc well-lit and is the lighting even   **AS 1428.2 Cl. 19*** |  |  |  |
| 1.21 | *Are direction signs to DAPB provided, if DAPB sign not visible from car park entry **AS / NZS 2890.6 – A3*** |  |  |  |
| 1.22 | *Are there appropriate directional TGSIs on any pathway adjacent to a DAPB, where a kerb ramp is at a mid-block section or not on a direct path of travel  **AS 1428.4.1 Cl. 3.1 (c) (i)*** |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

**Notes**

# **2.0	Change / Shower Facilities** {#2.0-change-/-shower-facilities}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 \- 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**Key Access Features**

It is important that adequate space is provided to allow two adults (a person with a disability and a carer) to use a change / shower area simultaneously and where possible that adult and baby change tables are also provided. 

Key access features also include provision of an accessible shower seat, appropriate handrails in the shower, unobstructed circulation space, level, slip resistant, step free floor surfaces, a vertical shower support grab rail, clothes hooks and / or lockers at an accessible height and an emergency alarm button within easy reach of the shower.

Unisex facilities are preferred and compliance with relevant Australian Standards is crucial, as many people with disabilities will not be able to use the facilities unless they are installed to minimum Standards. 

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

| Class of Building | Minimum accessible unisex showers to be provided |
| :---- | :---- |
| Class 1b | Not less than 1; and Where private accessible unisex showers are provided for an accessible bedroom, common accessible unisex showers need not be provided |
| Class 2 | Where showers are provided in common areas, not less than 1 |
| Class 3 and Class 9c aged care building | In every accessible sole-occupancy unit provided with showers within the accessible sole-occupancy unit, not less than 1; and 1 for every 10 showers or part thereof provided in common areas |
| Class 5, 6, 7, 8 and 9 – except for within a ward area of a Class 9a health-care building | Where clause F2.3 of the BCA requires 1 or more showers, not less than 1 for every 10 showers or part thereof |
| Class 10a – except: a)	a Class 10a 	appurtenant to 	another class of 	building; and b)	a sanitary 	compartment 	dedicated to a 	single caravan / 	camping site | Where showers are provided, 1 for every 10 showers or part thereof |

**Source: *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010***

Showers recesses and circulation space are required to provide a minimum circulation space (1600mm wide and 2350mm long \- two walled enclosure, 1600mm wide x 2500mm long three walled enclosure). Wet areas within that space shall be a minimum of 1160mm x 1100mm. In addition it requires appropriate grade floor surfaces, fixtures and fittings, including a seat, soap holder, clothes hooks that are easily accessible for a person using a wheelchair. 

**Checklist**

| 2 | Change / Shower Facilities          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 2.1 | Is there a designated accessible shower cubicle for people using wheelchairs **(requirement dependant on class of building under APS)** **APS – F2.4 (b) NOTE: can still be considered under equity requirements of DDA**  |  |  |  |
| 2.2 | **If** two or more shower recesses are provided, is at least one of the opposite hand  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.1 (c)** |  |  |  |
| 2.3 | Does the shower doorway have a min. clear opening width of 850mm   **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.2** |  |  |  |
| 2.4 | Does the door / doorframe into the shower area have a min. luminance contrast of 30% to the adjacent surfaces  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.1** |  |  |  |
| 2.5 | **If** an inward opening shower door is provided, is it operable or removable from outside in an emergency **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.2.9 (b)** |  |  |  |
| 2.6 | Is the shower circulation space a min. size of 1600mm x 2500mm for a three walled enclosure, or 1600mm x 2350mm for a two walled enclosure **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.1 / 12.5.3** |  |  |  |
| 2.7 | Is the shower recess accessible with no hob or step and at a gradient of between1:60 and 1:80 **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.2** |  |  |  |
| 2.8 | Is the slope of the remainder of the sanitary facility provided at a grade of between 1:80 and 1:100  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.2** |  |  |  |
| 2.9 | Is the circulation space clear to a height of not less than 2000mm (excluding allowable fittings) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.1 (a)** |  |  |  |
| 2.10 | Are there appropriate grab rails (30 – 40mm dia.) available at 800 – 810mm high (back wall) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.4** |  |  |  |
| 2.11 | Is there a showerhead support grab rail (vertical 30 – 40mm dia.) installed with the bottom end between 1000 – 1100 and the top end between 1880 – 1900mm high (Note: optional extension available) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5. / 14**  |  |  |  |
| 2.12 | Is the vertical showerhead support grab rail located 580 – 600mm from the internal corner of the shower **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5. / 14** |  |  |  |
| 2.13 | Is a foldable, self-draining, slip resistant seat (960mm x 390 / 400mm) provided in the shower recess at a height of 470 – 480mm, with an appropriate clearance from adjacent surfaces (i.e. 40mm max.)(requires rounded edges and must fold upwards – refer AS) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.9** |  |  |  |

| 2 | Change / Shower Facilities          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 2.14 | Is the shower seat able to withstand a force of 1100N **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.9** |  |  |  |
| 2.15 | **If** the shower seat is in the folded up position, is the grab rail accessible **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.9**  |  |  |  |
| 2.16 | Are the drainage gaps / slots within the shower seat 4 – 6mm wide **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.9** |  |  |  |
| 2.17 | Is a hand held and adjustable shower head available within reach when seated **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.6** |  |  |  |
| 2.18 | Is a flexible hose provided for the shower that is a min. length of 1500mm (Note: requirements of back flow prevention device) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.6** |  |  |  |
| 2.19 | Is the floor slip resistant **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |
| 2.20 | Is the tap/s located on the wall at a height between 900 – 1100mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.2.1** |  |  |  |
| 2.21 | Is the hot tap located on the left of / or above the cold tap **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.2.1** |  |  |  |
| 2.22 | Are the tap handles lever or sensor control or voice activated **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.2.1**  |  |  |  |
| 2.23 | **If** the taps have lever handles, are they located more than 50mm from adjacent surfaces and nor more than 100mm long **AS 1428.1 – Cl. 12.2.1/12.5.8** |  |  |  |
| 2.24 | Is the tap fixture located no closer than 50mm from the vertical grab rail (to ensure clearance around grab rail) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.8** |  |  |  |
| 2.25 | *Are the taps clearly identified as hot and cold (colour and text)* |  |  |  |
| 2.26 | Is there a soap holder located between 900 – 1100mm no closer than 50mm of the vertical support rail (protruding type preferred) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.7** |  |  |  |
| 2.27 | Are a minimum of two clothes hanging devices provided at 1200 \- 1350mm high, with one within 390 – 410mm and the 2nd within 590 – 610mm of the folding seat and not less than 500mm out from any internal corner **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.4.4 / 12.5.1**  |  |  |  |

| 2 | Change / Shower Facilities          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 2.28 | **If** there is a baby change table available, is it at a height of 820mm with leg clearance height underneath of 720mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.2.8.2** |  |  |  |
| 2.29 | **If** the waste outlet is in the centre line of the shower floor, is it (525 \- 575mm from the wall with tap / 555 – 605mm from the wall with the seat) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 12.5.2 (b) (**Note: A linear drain may be provided) |  |  |  |

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

# **3.0	Children’s Service Centres** {#3.0-children’s-service-centres}

**Relevant Australian Standards and Regulations:**

**AS 1428.1 \- 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for** 

			**access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS1428.3 \-  1992                   Design for access and mobility – Requirements for children and adolescents with physical disabilities *(Obsolescent)***

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Relevant Reference:** State and Commonwealth Children’s Services Centre Regulations

**Key Access Features**  
Both adults and children with disabilities will require access to Children’s Services Centres. Parents, grandparents, children or staff may have a variety of access needs and consideration should to be given to all of these.  
   
State and/or Commonwealth Children’s Services Centre Regulations detail specific requirements that must be met, in order for a facility to be registered to operate as a preschool or child care centre. 

Many of these regulations relate to the safety of children and are mandatory, e.g. child proof gate. Some of the regulations will create access barriers for some people, particularly people with mobility challenges. For example, the need for a childproof gate at the front entry of the centre to ensure children cannot get out onto the road is essential, however a person who uses a wheelchair, is of short stature or has dexterity issues, may have difficulty independently using the gate.

Alternatives such as intercoms or door bells as well as automated door openers should be provided. Staff support will sometimes be required and it is essential that staff are aware of the barriers that may prevent independent access.

Other key access issues include provision of accessible car parking, toilets for both children and adults, emergency assembly areas, access to and onto playground equipment, colour contrasts, acoustic materials to reduce noise and glare free lighting, particularly for babies who spend a lot of time on their backs looking up at light.  
**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**  
An accessway (CAPT) is required to and into the area.

**Checklist**

| 3 | Children’s Services Centres          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 3.1 | *Is there access to the main **internal play** area providing a min. clear space of 2250 x 2250mm to allow circulation for a 360° wheelchair turn (a space of 2450 x 2450mm is preferred) **AS 1428.2 Cl. 6.3*** |  |  |  |
| 3.2 | *Are accessible toilet pans provided for children with disabilities, at a height of 315 \- 335mm for ambulant children with disabilities, and at a height of 460 \- 480mm for children using wheelchairs **AS 1428.3 Cl. 10.1 / 10.2*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |
| 3.3 | *Are accessible washbasins provided for children with disabilities, at a height of 640 \- 660mm for ambulant children with disabilities, and at a height of 705 \- 725mm for children using wheelchairs **AS 1428.3 Cl. 10.3*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |
| 3.4 | *Is appropriate clearance provided below the washbasin suitable for wheelchair access for a child **AS 1428.3 Cl. 10.4*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |
| 3.5 | *Are drinking fountain controls provided at appropriate heights that are easy to use for children of each age group **AS 1428.3 Cl. 12.1*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |
| 3.6 | *Are taps provided that are easy to operate for children of each age group **AS 1428.3 Cl. 12.3*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |
| 3.7 | *Do door closers to be used by children, require a force less than 2.9N to open from 0 \- 90° **AS 1428.3 Cl. 12.1 / 12.2*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |

| 3.11 | *Do the 1:14 ramps have landings every 2.2 metres (or 1:17 every 3.5m, or 1:22 every 4.2m) (Note; requirements of changes in direction) **AS 1428.3 Cl. 7*** **Obsolescent** |  |  |  |

| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |

# **4.0	Contrasts** {#4.0-contrasts}

**Relevant Australian Standards**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Relevant References**

* Vision Australia Guidelines  
* CRC Wayfinding Guidelines  
* Wayfound Victoria

**Key Access Features**

The use of luminance, colour and textural contrasts within the built environment maximises accessibility for people with low vision who may have difficulty interpreting objects, fixtures, fittings, changes in surfaces and clear paths of travel. 

Luminance contrast is required in many locations and is preferred to colour contrast alone. Luminance contrast refers to the difference in the light / dark properties of two adjacent surfaces rather than just their colours. It is luminance contrast that is important to enhancing vision, because it offers light / dark differences that can be picked up more easily by people with low vision. For example, cherry red on black has a high colour contrast but low luminance contrast, and is not as visible as pale pink or yellow on black to people with low vision. 

The use of luminance and colour contrast is very helpful in assisting people with low vision to locate important aspects of the environment such as poles, bollards, furniture, doors and doorways (particularly glass doors), signs, handrails and other objects of interest. Contrast can also be used to highlight potential hazards such as the edges of steps, a roadway or poles in streetscapes and play areas. 

Textural contrast can also be helpful such as tactile markers that people can identify by feel. Tactile ground surface indicators commonly seen at the edges of railway platforms are a good example of this. Other examples include carpet matting on a vinyl floor surface and domed buttons on handrails to indicate the end of the stairway or ramp is approaching. 

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

Luminance contrasts are required to meet Australian Standards:

* where Tactile Ground Surface Indicators (TGSIs) are installed – required levels of contrast vary from 30% to 60% dependant on the installation type;  
* at doorways (minimum width 50mm) – door and door jamb; door leaf and adjacent wall; architrave and wall; door leaf and architrave; or door jamb and adjacent wall;  
* to signage where required;  
* to a toilet seat within a unisex accessible toilet;  
* lighting is required to some signage to ensure it maintains its luminance contrast at night.


Warning Tactile Ground Surface Indicators are to be provided to warn a person with low vision that they are approaching:

* stairways (excluding fire isolated stairways);  
* an escalator;  
* a passenger conveyor or moving walk;  
* a ramp (excluding fire isolated ramps, a step ramps, a kerb ramp or a swimming pool ramp);  
* an overhead obstruction less than 2m (in the absence of a suitable barrier \-  other than a doorway);  
* level transitions between a vehicular way adjacent to a pedestrian entrance to a building.

An appropriate solid contrasting strip (min. 75mm with bottom edge at a height of 900 – 1000mm) is required to any frameless or fully glazed doorway and sidelights, or fully glazed wall that is capable of being mistaken as a door or entry (strip must be viewable from 2m either side.  This may require a difference between the internal and external strips).

A raised tactile warning is required at some handrail installations (e.g. aged care centres).

**Checklist**

If the following elements are incorporated into the building, is there a **clear contrast between the element and the background surface** and / or the surrounding area:

# **5.0	Customer Service Areas** {#5.0-customer-service-areas}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 \- 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010		Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**Key Access Features**

Wide self opening doors with step free entry and a continuous accessible path of travel to any customer service counter are important considerations in any customer service area.

Installation of low height reception counters, incorporating adequate leg clearance is essential. If high counters are installed, many users with disabilities, particularly a person who may be seated, may not effectively be able to undertake a conversation with staff. They may in fact be excluded, whilst staff talk with a friend or carer who is standing at eye level.

Consideration should also be given to the provision of other furniture that allows a person using a wheelchair or an older adult ease of access. Tables with leg clearance underneath, circulation space around and between furniture and fittings, and colour contrast with background, dimensions and supports such as backs and armrests. D or D lever style handles on any cupboards assist all users. 

Other key access elements include provision of internal accessways free from any obstructions such as pot plants, seating or displays. Controls for doors, switches, power points, security alarm pads etc. should provide ease of use for a person using a wheelchair or with a manipulatory disability.

Pamphlets and brochures provided in accessible locations and at accessible heights for people of short stature or using a wheelchair.

Clear directional signage indicating the various service areas as well as hearing augmentation and consistent even lighting are also required. 

Appropriate hearing augmentation including Assistive Listening Systems and supports, should be available for people who are Deaf or hard of hearing. Inclusion of acoustic design elements in new or refurbished projects will assist in providing interior spaces that are responsive to the hearing needs of older persons, or people who are Deaf or hard of hearing. 

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to and through the area

Hearing augmentation to be provided:

* at any screened reception counter, ticket office, teller’s booth at which the public are separated.

![Access Cartoons 023.tif][image2]

**Checklist**

| 5 | Customer Service Areas          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| ----- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 5.1 | **If** there is a reception area, is there a direct CAPT from the PPE to the reception counter area **APS – DP1** |  |  |  |
| 5.2 | *Does the reception counter / ticket or tellers booth provide a wheelchair accessible section at a height of 830 – 870mm with leg clearance at a height of 800 – 840mm underneath, for a min. length of 900mm  **AS 1428.2 Cl. 24.1.1*** |  |  |  |
| 5.3 | Does any screened reception counter / ticket or tellers booth, with an inbuilt amplification system, have a hearing augmentation system installed **APS – DP9 / D3.6** |  |  |  |
| 5.4 | Is the floor surface slip resistant **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |
| 5.5 | **If** carpeted, is it short pile (\<11mm and backing \<4mm) and securely attached to the floor surface **APS – Amdt. 1** |  |  |  |
| 5.6 | Are any exposed edges of carpet fastened to the floor surface and have a trim along the entire length of the exposed edge **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.3.1** |  |  |  |
| 5.7 | *Is some seating provided 450 – 520mm high, with armrests at a height of 220 – 300mm above the seat and a seat back, for use in the customer service area **AS 1428.2 Cl. 27.2*** |  |  |  |
| 5.8 | *Is the customer service area appropriately lit and is the lighting even	 **AS 1428.2 Cl. 19*** |  |  |  |
| 5.9 | *Are display and information stands within common reach ranges (230 – 1350mm) for wheelchair users (Note: different angles of approach e.g. side approach) **AS 1428.2 Cl. 22*** |  |  |  |
| 5.10 | Are internal walkways a min. of 1000mm wide (1200mm preferred)  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.3** |  |  |  |
| 5.11 | *Are there accessible height security alarm pads* |  |  |  |
| 5.12 | *Are there effective contrasts between vertical and horizontal surfaces / objects* |  |  |  |

| 5.14 | *Is there effective uniform lighting to the area*  |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

# **6.0	Entrances** {#6.0-entrances}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021	Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work**   
**AS 1428.2 \- 1992	Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**  
**AS 1428.5 \- 2010	Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**  
**Key Access Features**

Principal pedestrian entrances shall provide wide, level, step free access for use by all people. These may include a level / flat transition or ramp from an adjoining path or walkway. An accessible entry should not incorporate any steps, stairs or turnstiles or other impediment that inhibits its independent use by a person with a disability or a person using a mobility aid such as a pram or delivery trolley. 

Automatic self opening / closing doors are preferred that incorporate motion and presence sensors, to ensure people do not get caught whilst the doors are operating and the use of automatic doors where the depth of the recess at the door is greater than 300mm will assist all users.

Other key access elements include provision of contrasting strips across any glass doors for ease of recognition, colour contrasts to frames, circulation spaces at entry points (inside and outside), alarm pads or card controls at an accessible height and clear concise signage indicating the entry and direction to facilities. 

Appropriate hearing augmentation including Assistive Listening Systems and supports, should also be available for people who are Deaf or hard of hearing at security points and intercoms.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

* access is required through the principal pedestrian entrance and not less than 50% of all pedestrian entrances (including the principal pedestrian entrance);  
* multiple doorway installation requirements vary;  
* a building \>500m² is required to provide an accessible entrance not more than 50m away from an inaccessible entrance;  
* a clear opening width of a min. 850mm at any doorway, including the active leaf of a multiple leaf door (except an automatic opening door) is required;  
* an appropriate solid contrasting strip (min. 75mm with bottom edge at a height of 900 – 1000mm) is required to any frameless or fully glazed doorway and sidelights, or fully glazed wall that is capable of being mistaken as a door or entry (strip must be viewable from 2m either side);  
* signage is required at any non-accessible entrance directing users to an accessible entrance;  
* an appropriate level entry; threshold ramp or step ramp is required at accessible pedestrian entrances;  
* doors / doorframes etc., are to have a minimum luminance contrast of 30% to their adjacent surface.




![Access Cartoons 048.tif][image3]

**Checklist**

| 6 | Entrances                                 (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |

| 6.6 | **If** there are security entry controls (card / buttons / intercom) are these at 900 – 1100mm-grasped/turned, 900-1200mm-pushed, 900-1250mm (not less than 500mm from corner)-touched, (*ticket slot 800 – 900mm),* and easy to operate **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 / *AS 1428.2 Cl. 28*** |  |  |  |

| 6.13 | Are door handles (D style) on sliding doors not less than 60mm from each doorjamb **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 (d)** |  |  |  |

| 6 | Entrances                                 (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 6.14 | **If** an outward opening door is not self closing, is there a horizontal handrail or pull bar installed at a height between 900 – 1100mm (min. 50mm clearance from edge of door / door handle) on the inside of the door **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.2 (f)** |  |  |  |
| 6.15 | **If** doors are power operated, are the push button controls a min. of 25mm dia., proud of the surface (activating door before the button becomes level with surrounding surface)  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.4** |  |  |  |
| 6.16 | **If** doors are power operated, are the controls at least 500mm from an internal corner and between 500 – 1000mm from arch of the hinged door leaf (in any position) / or clear of a surface-mounted sliding door in the open position **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 (e)** |  |  |  |
| 6.17 | *Are the door handles provided with an appropriate luminance contrast **AS 1428.2 Cl. 23.3 (b)*** |  |  |  |
| 6.18 | *Do automatic self-opening doors have effective motion, and presence sensors installed* |  |  |  |
| 6.19 | **If** the doors / sidelights are frameless or fully glazed, are they clearly marked for safety and ease of identification across the full door width, with a solid and non-transparent contrasting line (viewable from 2m inside and outside) (luminance 30%). Size of line not less than 75mm high, with the lower edge at a height of 900 – 1000mm above finished floor level **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.6** |  |  |  |
| 6.20 | Do all the doors or doorframes have a min. luminance contrast of 30% to their adjacent surfaces **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.1** |  |  |  |
| 6.21 | Is the entrance door easy, to initially open, (no heavy closer or spring) 20N max. (4.3lbf)  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.2 (e)** |  |  |  |
| 6.22 | Is the min. **clear opening** of a doorway at the PPE 850mm or greater **APS – D3.2 (5) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.2** |  |  |  |
| 6.23 | **If** the doorway has 2 independent operated leaves, is the open doorway a min. of 850mm wide **APS – D3.2 (5) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.2** |  |  |  |
| 6.24 | Is the door threshold level or is there an appropriate threshold ramp available at the entry (i.e. no step, inappropriate mat, weather strip etc.) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.5 / 7.5** |  |  |  |
| 6.25 | **If** there is a threshold (max. rise 35mm) at the entrance or doorway (not more than 20mm from door leaf it serves), is there a ramp of not more than 280mm in length and min. ratio of 1:8. (Note: if the rise is greater a step ramp will be required) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.5** |  |  |  |

| 6 | Entrances                                 (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 6.26 | **If** the threshold ramp does not abut a wall or kerb, are sides tapered or splayed (min. 45°) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.5** |  |  |  |
| 6.27 | **If** there is a recessed mat within the CAPT is the abutment of the surfaces no more than 3mm if vertical or 5mm if bevelled (rounded) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.2** |  |  |  |
| 6.28 | **If** there is a carpet leading edge at the entrance is there a vertical face no higher than 3mm or a rounded bevelled edge no higher than 5mm or above that height a gradient of 1:8 up to a total max. height of 10mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.3.1**  |  |  |  |
| 6.29 | Is there appropriate wheelchair circulation space outside the entrance doorway (not steeper that 1:40) (Doorway circulations spaces may overlap other circulation spaces)    **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.3** |  |  |  |
| 6.30 | Is there appropriate wheelchair circulation space inside the entrance doorway (not steeper that 1:40) (Doorway circulations spaces may overlap other circulation spaces)    **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.3** |  |  |  |
| 6.31 | **If** there is an airlock, vestibule, or enclosed space, is there not less than 1450mm between the doorway (plus the door leaf width if the door encroaches into the space) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.3.5** |  |  |  |
| 6.32 | ***If** there is an alarm control pad, is it located at a height between 900 – 1200mm high, accessible and easy to operate* |  |  |  |
| 6.33 | ***If** there is a doorbell, is it accessible and easy to operate, located at a height between 900 – 1200mm*  |  |  |  |
| 6.34 | *Is there appropriate lighting at the PPE* |  |  |  |
| 6.35 | **If** there are glazed viewing panels in doors, is the lower edge of the glazing not more than 1000mm above FFL, upper edge not less than 1600mm above FFL,  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.7** |  |  |  |
| 6.36 | **If** there are glazed viewing panels in doors, is the width of the glazing within 200mm from latch edge of the door and  min 150mm wide  **AS 1428.1 Cl 3.7** |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **7.0	Emergency Egress / Evacuation** {#7.0-emergency-egress-/-evacuation}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010		Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**Key Access Features**

Accessible emergency egress from buildings is essential and should incorporate a continuous accessible path of travel to a place of safety leading away from the building.

Emergency exits should be well signed and provide step free egress along a continuous accessible path of travel to an emergency assembly area for all building users. Safe havens for people with disabilities, who may be on levels above the ground, should also be provided, as lifts will not be available for use in some emergencies such as fires.

Emergency alarms should be provided that incorporate audible and visible indicators to ensure a person with low vision or a person who is Deaf or hard of hearing can be alerted to emergency situations or security checkpoint signals. Clear concise signage regarding emergency procedures is also essential.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to any emergency exit door. 

**Checklist**

NOTE: If the emergency egress provisions of the building meet the requirements of the BCA, they are deemed to have met the requirements of the Premises Standards.

| 7 | Emergency Egress / Evacuation    (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 7.1 | *Is there an accessible (e.g. appropriate door handle, clear door opening width, opening force) emergency exit in addition to the main entry* |  |  |  |
| 7.2 | *Is there clear, visible, accessible signage on emergency exits* |  |  |  |
| 7.3 | *Is there a continuous accessible path of travel from the building to any nominated assembly area (e.g. firm path, no steps, stairs, well lit)* |  |  |  |
| 7.4 | *Are audible emergency alarms provided in the building* |  |  |  |
| 7.5 | *Are visible emergency alarms provided in the building* |  |  |  |
| 7.6 | *Are there places of refuge provided for people with mobility difficulties on levels above the main entrance level* |  |  |  |
| 7.7 | *Are audible security alarms provided at any security checkpoints* |  |  |  |
| 7.8 | *Are visible security alarms provided at any security checkpoints* |  |  |  |
| 7.9 | *Are any fire hoses and extinguishers located at 700 – 1200mm high*  |  |  |  |
| 7.10 | *Is the emergency management plan located at an accessible height in a public area in an accessible format (e.g. large print, tactile, Braille)* |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

**Notes**

# **8.0	Floor / Ground Surfaces** {#8.0-floor-/-ground-surfaces}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 4586 \- 2013 	Slip resistance classification of new pedestrian surface materials** 

**Key Access Features**

Firm and slip resistant floor and ground surfaces are required to and through a building. These surfaces need to be suitable in both wet and dry conditions and provide an effective contrast to adjoining surfaces.  Slip resistant is any surface that provides traction for a wheelchair or a person walking, in both wet and dry situations.

The following finishes are considered satisfactory (under AS 1428.1 2001), subject to the surface texture being traversable by a wheelchair:

For wet locations:

* concrete with abrasive or texture finish;  
* concrete with exposed aggregate finish;  
* bituminous concrete;  
* natural stone with rough finish;  
* paving bricks and special abrasive finish;  
* slip-resistant tiles.

For dry locations:

* all materials suitable for wet conditions (above);  
* short piled carpet;  
* smooth flooring materials which should not have a high gloss, slippery finish, or which have been suitably treated.


**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to all areas within a building required to be accessible, this incorporates the above key access features listed above.  
.

**Checklist**

| 8 | Floor / Ground Surfaces                (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 8.1 | Is the ground / floor surface firm and level (e.g. with no sharp transitions at abutting surfaces) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |
| 8.2 | Is the floor / ground surface slip resistant (in wet and dry conditions) allowing traction for a person using a wheelchair and people with ambulant or sensory disability **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |
| 8.3 | **If** carpeted, is it short pile (\<11mm and backing \<4mm) and securely attached to the floor surface **AS 1428.1 Cl 4.3** |  |  |  |
| 8.4 | *Does the floor / ground surface have effective contrasts to walls and doors / doorframes* |  |  |  |
| 8.5 | **If** timber decking boards are installed and are no greater than 150mm wide, is there a maximum 6mm gap between boards **AS 1428.1 Cl 4.5** |  |  |  |
| 8.6 | **If** timber decking boards are installed that are over 150mm wide, is there a maximum gap of 10mm between boards, and if the gap is over 8mm do the boards run transverse to the direction of travel **AS 1428.1 Cl 4.5** |  |  |  |
| 8.7 | **If** timber decking boards are installed, are adjacent boards  level with a maximum vertical 3mm tolerance **AS 1428.1 Cl 4.5** |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement* –   
**NOTE**: The BCA requires a prescribed level of slip resistance at stairways, ramps and landings

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

**Notes**

# **9.0	Hearing Augmentation** {#9.0-hearing-augmentation}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021	Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010	 Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992	Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**Key Access Features**

Hearing augmentation is important for people who are Deaf or hard of hearing in order to support participation in a range of activities. Assistive listening systems are important in any area where people who are Deaf or hard of hearing wish to hear effectively, this may include areas where meetings, presentations, lectures, theatre, sporting and leisure events or similar activities are to be held. They should also be installed at customer service counters, teller’s cash booths and lifts.

A hearing augmentation system should always be provided in a space where a sound amplification system (e.g. speaker system) is installed. The area covered by the hearing augmentation system shall include appropriate signage for ease of identification by users.

Some assistive listening systems can be built into a facility, whilst others are portable and can be moved from room to room. 

Other considerations to assist a person who is Deaf or hard of hearing whilst using a building include, provision of acoustic design elements that assist in reducing background noise particularly in indoor areas such as reception counters, public meeting areas, social interchange points, information and cashier areas. These elements could include 

* rubber tips on furniture legs;  
* soft furnishings;  
* low pile carpet;  
* heavy curtains and wall hangings;  
* automatic doors closures;  
* double glazing on windows;  
* use of shrubs, trees or high, solid fences to limit traffic noise;  
* provision of quiet areas for conversations with users;  
* quiet air conditioners, fans and office equipment;  
* acoustic treatments to walls and ceilings.

Seating that provides good lines of sight to speakers, glare free surfaces to assist the audience with lip reading is also important, as well as adequate light for sign language interpreters to be seen easily.

Visible emergency alarms throughout the building, as well as at security checkpoints are also important.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

Hearing augmentation to be provided where an inbuilt amplification system is installed (other than one used only for emergency warning) 

* in a room in a class 9b building; or  
* at any ticket office, teller’s booth, reception area or the like, where the public is screened from the service provider; or  
* in meeting rooms, auditoriums, conference rooms and any room used for judicatory purposes in a class 9b building;  
* available between 80 – 95% of the space dependant on the system type;  
* signage is to be provided to inform users of availability of system and location of receivers if required;  
* any screen or scoreboard associated with a Class 9b building and capable of displaying public announcements must be capable of supplementing any public address system, other than a public address system used for emergency warning purposes only.

**Checklist**

| 9 | Hearing Augmentation                     (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 9.1 | **If** a sound amplification system is installed / inbuilt is there a hearing augmentation system that covers 80% of the total enclosed space if an induction loop is inbuilt, or 95% if a receiver system in use **APS – D3.7 (1) (2) (3)** |  |  |  |
| 9.2 | Is hearing augmentation available at any screened / enclosed reception area / ticket or tellers cash booth (that has an inbuilt amplification system) **APS – D3.7 (1) (2) (3)** |  |  |  |
| 9.3 | *Is hearing augmentation available in meeting rooms (seating 5 or more participants) **AS 1428.5 \- 3*** |  |  |  |
| 9.4 | *Is hearing augmentation available in any lift to assist with communication in an emergency **AS 1428.5 \- 3*** |  |  |  |
| 9.5 | Does signage, including the international symbol of deafness, indicate the area where an assistive listening system is operational and the area covered **APS – D3.6 (b) (i) / D4 / D3.7 (1) (2) (3) / AS 1428.1 Cl 5.2.2** |  |  |  |
| 9.6 | Does signage, including the international symbol of deafness, indicate which type of system is in place **APS – D3.6 (b) (ii) / D4 / D3.7 (1) (2) (3) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 5.2.2** |  |  |  |
| 9.7 | **If** receivers are being used, does the signage indicate where the receivers can be obtained **APS D3.6 (b) (iii)** |  |  |  |
| 9.8 | **If** a screen or scoreboard is capable of displaying public announcements, is it capable of supplementing any public address system (other than a system used for emergency warning purposes only)  **APS – D3.7 (4)** |  |  |  |
| 9.9 | *Is appropriate seating with backs and armrests available that provides good lines of sight for lip reading* |  |  |  |
| 9.10 | *Are there acoustic design elements to reduce noise e.g. rubber tips on furniture legs, soft furnishings, low pile carpet, double glazing, quiet equipment etc.* |  |  |  |
| 9.11 | *Are there visible alarms at any security checkpoint  **AS 1428.5 \- 3*** |  |  |  |
| 9.12 | *Are there visible emergency alarms throughout the building* |  |  |  |
| 9.13 | *Is there effective lighting for lip reading and sign language interpreters* |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **10.0	Internal Accessways** {#10.0-internal-accessways}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features**

Internal accessways shall provide adequate turning and passing space for two people to easily pass each other when coming from opposite directions, including a person using a mobility aid. These areas shall be kept clear of obstructions such as built \- in seating, pot plants and rubbish bins. An effective contrast between the walls and floor surface will assist people with low vision in orientation.

Other key access features include level, step free, slip resistant surfaces in good repair, appropriate lighting and adequate overhead clearance for the full length of the walkway or corridor. Alternatives to any steps shall be provided such as a ramp, which incorporate appropriate handrails, kerbs and tactile ground surface indicators to Australian Standards

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

* signage is required at any non-accessible entrance directing users to an accessible entrance  
* an accessway (CAPT) is required to all parts of the building required to be accessible  
* appropriate doorway circulation spaces are required (dimensions vary dependant on angle of approach and door operation)  
* turning and passing spaces are to be provided where there is no direct line of sight available to the end of a walkway / corridor and where it is not possible to continue along the walkway / corridor.  Configurations vary  
* all switches and controls on a CAPT (other than general purpose outlets) are to be installed at specific heights with dimension and distance requirements at corners and doorways  
* door controls in, or forming part of a CAPT are required to ensure that a person can unlock and open them with one hand, with consideration given to the type of door furniture and the distances required from adjoining and background surfaces. The weight of the door is also to be considered

Where works are being undertaken within an existing building that requires a building approval, a continuous accessible path of travel is required from the principal pedestrian entry to the new building works. These works are referred to as the ‘affected part’.

![Access Cartoons 046.tif][image4]

**Checklist** 

| 10 | Internal Accessways                   (tick relevant box) |  | Y |  | N |  | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 10.1 | Does the accessway have a min. width of 1000mm i.e. structurally and maintained to remain clear of temporary obstructions e.g. pot plants, bins  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.3** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.2 | Does the full length of the accessway have an overhead clearance of 2000mm (1980mm allowed at doorway) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.2** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.3 | Do accessways provide a passing space where a direct line of sight is not available to the end of the walkway (max. 20m intervals) (min. 1800mm wide x 2000mm long)  **APS – D3.3 (c) (d) (e) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.4** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.4 | Do accessways provide a turning space near the end of the walkway where it is not possible to continue (within 2m of end)  **APS – D3.3 (c) (d) (e) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.5** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.5 | **If** a change of direction is required, is there appropriate circulation space provided along the accessway for the angle of the turn **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.5** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.6 | Does the accessway have a slip-resistant surface with a texture that is traversable by a wheelchair  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.7 | **If** there is a non accessible entrance doorway, is there appropriate signage provided (int. Symbol, direction arrow) directing users to an accessible entrance **APS – D3.6 (e) AS 1428.1 CL 5** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.8 | Is the min. clear opening of a doorway on any accessway 850mm or greater **APS – D3.2 (5) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.2** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.9 | Is there appropriate wheelchair circulation space outside the doorway (**NOTE**: 1:40 grade, additional considerations at surface mounted sliding doors) (Doorway circulation space may overlap other circulation spaces) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.3** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.10 | Is there appropriate wheelchair circulation space inside the doorway (**NOTE**: 1:40 grade, additional considerations at surface mounted sliding doors) (Doorway circulation space may overlap other circulation spaces) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.3** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.11 | Can the door be unlocked and opened by one hand (i.e. D or D lever handles) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.2 (a)** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.12 | Is the clearance between the handle and the back plate or door face (at the centre grip section) not less than 35mm and not more than 45mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.2 (b)** |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.13 | Are all door controls (handles) that need to be grasped or turned between 900 – 1100mm high **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 (a)** |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 10 | Internal Accessways                   (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 10.14 | Are all door controls that need to be pushed between 900 – 1200mm high **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 (b)** |  |  |  |
| 10.15 | Are all door controls that only need to be touched between 900 – 1250mm high (and not less than 500mm from an internal corner, except as specified in AS 1735.12) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 10.4.3 (c)** |  |  |  |
| 10.16 | **If** doors are power operated, are the controls at least 500mm from an internal corner and between 1000 – 2000mm from the hinged swing door leaf (in any position) / or doorway of sliding door  **AS 1428.1 Cl.10.4.3 (e)** |  |  |  |

| 10.21 | Are all switches and controls provided on a CAPT (other than general purpose outlets (GPOs)) located at a height of 900 – 1100mm and not less than 500mm from an internal corner **AS 1428.1 Cl 11.1**  |  |  |  |

# **11.0	Kerb Ramps** {#11.0-kerb-ramps}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features**

Kerb ramps are necessary to provide an accessible transition between pathways or other features of the built environment, such as parking bays, to / from adjoining pathways, road crossing points or other uneven ground surfaces. Usually, each kerb ramp shall have an opposite kerb ramp, directly in line with the path of travel. This supports provision of an effective continuous accessible path of travel and ease of access particularly for a person using a wheelchair or other mobility aid. It also assists a person with low vision to find their way through an area more easily. 

Kerb ramps at road crossing points that lead users to steps or stairs only are not recommended.

Other key access features include provision of tactile ground surface indicators at kerb ramps as per Australian Standards, sloping sides on kerb ramps, alignment with adjacent medians, property boundaries or building lines, firm slip resistant surfaces, appropriate lighting.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 20*10 and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required from the allotment boundary, car parking area (incorporating a designated accessible parking bay) and an adjoining accessible building (connected by a pedestrian link), which may incorporate the key access elements listed above.

**Checklist**

| 11 | Kerb Ramps                                  (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 11.1 | **If** the pathway on the accessway crosses any vehicle traffic areas, (e.g. parking lot, internal road) is it free from any changes in level (e.g. kerbs, steps etc.) **AS 1428.1. Cl. 4** |  |  |  |
| 11.2 | Is the ground surface on the kerb ramp slip resistant **AS 1428.1. Cl. 4 / 7.7.3** |  |  |  |
| 11.3 | **If** the kerb ramps are inserted into the pathway, has the pathway width been extended to accommodate the kerb ramp **AS / NZS 2890.6 \- Cl. 2.2.2 / 2.5** |  |  |  |
| 11.4 | **If** there is an opposing kerb ramp / pedestrian refuge / median, are the centre lines of the kerb ramps aligned **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.7.1** |  |  |  |
| 11.5 | Do the kerb ramps on the accessway, have a max. rise of 190mm, length of 1520mm and do they have a slope / gradient where the ratio is not greater than 1:8 **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.7.2** |  |  |  |
| 11.6 | Are the openings of the kerb ramps a min. of 1000mm wide **AS 1428.1. Cl. 3.3** |  |  |  |
| 11.7 | Do the kerb ramps, on the pathway to the PPE, have a smooth transition between the road and the pathway (max. diff. 5mm with rounded or bevelled edge)  |  |  |  |
| 11.8 | Do the kerb ramps have an appropriate side profile i.e. splayed or tapered 45° **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.7.2** |  |  |  |
| 11.9 | Is the angle between the ramp surface and the lower surface (i.e. base of kerb) provided at an angle of 166° **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.7.2** |  |  |  |
| 11.10 | *Are there any TGSIs (hazard) indicators installed at kerb ramps on the accessway (width x 600 – 800mm, setback 300mm ± 10mm)*  |  |  |  |
| 11.11 | Do kerb ramps on the pathway have a landing of 1200mm min in length at the top and bottom of the ramp (following direction of travel) **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.8.3** |  |  |  |
| 11.12 | Do kerb ramps on the pathway have a landing of 1500mm x 2000mm at any change of direction (T junction) **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.8.3** |  |  |  |
| 11.13 | Do kerb ramps on the pathway have a landing of 1500mm x 1500mm at any single change of direction **AS 1428.1. Cl. 7.8.3** |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **12.0	Kitchen / Dining / Canteen Areas** {#12.0-kitchen-/-dining-/-canteen-areas}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**Key Access Features**

Independent equitable access should be provided to all utility areas within buildings for both visitors and staff. Inbuilt fixtures and fittings should be suitable for a person using a wheelchair to access, and incorporate low height areas with leg clearance underneath. Contrasts should be incorporated to provide definitions between vertical, horizontal and background surfaces for ease of recognition.

Adequate circulation space should be provided in kitchen, dining and canteen areas for a person using a wheelchair to easily enter, move around and independently access benches, sinks and other equipment as necessary. 

Low height counters should also be provided at canteen windows for staff and customers to adequately converse and reach items for sale. Equipment such as kettles, inbuilt hot water taps, stoves etc should be accessible by a person who is seated.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to be provided to and through the area.

**Checklist**

| 12 | Kitchen / Dining / Canteen Areas  (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 12.1 | Is there a CAPT provided to the kitchen / bar / dining / laundry / canteen area **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3** |  |  |  |
| 12.2 | *Does the counter have a wheelchair accessible section at a height between 830 – 870mm for a min. length of 900mm **AS 1428.2 Cl. 24*** |  |  |  |
| 12.3 | *Does the counter have at the wheelchair accessible section, a leg clearance underneath at a height between 800 – 840mm for a min. length of 900mm **AS 1428.2 Cl. 24*** |  |  |  |
| 12.4 | *Is the sink / basin accessible to people in wheelchairs (height 770 – 800mm) **AS 1428.2- A5*** |  |  |  |
| 12.5 | *Is the sink / basin accessible to people in wheelchairs (leg clearance height underneath 640-650mm) with appropriate unobstructed circulation space **AS 1428.2- A5*** |  |  |  |
| 12.6 | Is there a continuous internal accessible path of travel to any canteen window **APS – 2.2 (4) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 3** |  |  |  |
| 12.7 | ***If** there is a canteen / servery window does it have a wheelchair accessible section at a height between 830 – 870mm with a leg clearance underneath at a height of 800 – 840mm for a min. length of 900mm **AS 1428.2 Cl. 24*** |  |  |  |
| 12.8 | Is there a continuous external accessible path of travel to any external canteen / servery window  **APS – 2.2 (4) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 3** |  |  |  |
| 12.9 | *Are the operative components of any vending machine, for pre-packaged food and drink, accessible and between 700 – 1200mm high **AS 1428.2 Cl. 29*** |  |  |  |
| 12.10 | ***If** seating is available, is it at a height of 450 – 520mm with armrests located at a height between220 – 300mm above the seat and backs **AS 1428.2 Cl. 27.2*** |  |  |  |
| 12.11 | ***If** tea and coffee facilities are provided (other than vending machine), are the highest operable components located at a height between 900 – 1100mm* |  |  |  |
| 12.12 | Is there appropriate circulation space within the kitchen area, to enable a user ease of use for all facilities **APS – 2.2 (4) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 3** |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **13.0	Landscaping**  {#13.0-landscaping}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**Key Access Features**

Landscape designs, materials, plants, etc., should contribute to pedestrian safety. Avoid planting of species adjacent to pathways and car parking areas that develop overhanging foliage, and / or leaves / seeds that fall, as they can create difficulties for users.

Overflow of mulch, sap droppings, seed pods, berries, leaf and bark litter can create hazards for all users, particularly people with low vision or mobility impairments, especially in wet weather. Adequate overhead clearance shall be maintained above paved or occupied open areas.

Consideration should be given to plants that can assist users with way finding through an area. Plantings that provide orientation or direction cues for people with low vision, by incorporating distinctive scents, sounds, appearance or texture can be useful.

Dense plantings around passive rest areas can result in a feeling of isolation, particularly for younger children, older persons and people with disabilities and should be avoided. 

Lines of sight from seating to play areas for children should be available at all times. Landscaping should be appropriately maintained to ensure this is provided.

**Checklist**

| 13 | Landscaping                  (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 13.1 | *Are pathways free from plant species that develop overhanging foliage, and / or leaves or drop seed pods, berries, leaf and bark litter*  |  |  |  |
| 13.2 | *Are there landscape designs, materials, plants, etc., that contribute to pedestrian safety* |  |  |  |
| 13.3 | *Are any plantings used to provide orientation or direction cues for people with vision impairment e.g. distinctive scents, sounds, appearance or texture* |  |  |  |
| 13.4 | *Are any planter boxes appropriately located clear of any pathway* |  |  |  |
| 13.5 | *Are any dense plantings maintained to provide a clear line of sight* |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

**Notes**

# **14.0a, b, c	Lifts \- Passenger**  {#14.0a,-b,-c-lifts---passenger}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010	Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**AS 1735			Suite of Standards 	Lifts, escalators and moving walks**  

**Key Access Features**

Ideally, passenger lifts should be provided in all premises with more than one level (see APS / BCA for exemptions / limitations). They shall incorporate sufficient space to allow a person using a mobility aid, to comfortably enter and access the operational components including lift buttons with tactile elements and emergency intercoms etc. Handrails, tactile markings to lift buttons and signage shall also be provided. 

In some instances, particularly in retrofitting situations, it may be necessary to consider installation of platform lifts or stair climbers. These are not preferred in new facilities. 

Access to areas such as stages and swimming pools should incorporate appropriate ramp access.

Other key access features for lifts include auditory, tactile and visual considerations e.g. contrasts, glare free walls and controls, appropriate print size of controls and instructions.   Carpets that have a short pile length, appropriate door open dwell time to allow people to enter and exit safely, audio announcement of floor levels, and hearing augmentation to support communication for a person who are Deaf or hard of hearing in an emergency, must also be considered.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**  
Accepted lift types

| Lift Type | Limitations on use |
| :---- | :---- |
| AS1735.1 – appendix a | No limitation |
| AS1745.2 – electric passenger lift | No limitation |
| AS1735.3 electrohydraulic lift | No limitation |
| AS1735.7 stairway platform lift | Must not: Be used to serve a space in a building accommodating more than 100 persons calculated according to Clause D1.13 of the BCA; or Be used in a high traffic public use area such as a theatre, cinema, auditorium, transport interchange, shopping centre or the like; or Connect more than 2 storeys; or Where more than 1 stairway lift is installed, serve more than 2 consecutive storeys; or When in the folded position, encroach on the minimum width of a stairway required by clause D1.6 of the BCA |
| AS1735.8 inclined lift | No limitation |
| AS1735.14 low rise platform lift | Must not travel more than 1000mm |
| AS1735.15 lift for persons with limited mobility | Must not: For an enclosed type, travel more than 4m; or For an unenclosed type, travel more than 2m; or Be used in high traffic public use areas in buildings such as a theatre, cinema, auditorium, transport interchange, shopping complex or the like |

**Source – *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010***  
A floor dimension of 1400mm x 1600mm is required to a standard passenger lift (travelling over 12m). Requirements for other lifts vary dependant on the type of installation.  Refer to *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* for further detail.

A variety of features are required within the passenger lifts, these are specific to the type of installation provided. 

Lifts that travel over 2 floors require an audible announcement.

**NOTE:	Under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010*, the Access Code requires that a passenger lift have a floor dimension of not less than 1400mm x 1600mm (if travelling over 12m or 1100mm x 1400mm if travelling not more than 12m). This however, does not apply to a passenger lift that is in a new part or an affected part of an existing building if the lift travels more than 12m and has a lift floor that is not less than 1100mm x 1400mm.  Refer to *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* for further details.  For lifts that travel over 2 floors, an audible announcement is required.**

**![Access Cartoons 039.tif][image5]**

# **15.0	Meeting Spaces** {#15.0-meeting-spaces}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010		Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired recommendations**

**Key Access Features**

A continuous accessible path of travel should be provided to and through any meeting area. Consideration should also be given to provision of appropriate seating which allows integrated wheelchair spaces and access at various locations within the area. Issues such as provision of seats with backrests and armrests, lines of sight for viewing and proximity to emergency exits and toilets are also important. 

Other key access features include provision of appropriate access to any stage or podium area, installation of hearing augmentation systems in any meeting spaces that seat 5 or more people, incorporating signage to indicate the space covered by the system and highlighting the edge of any stage or podium edge to assist identification, particularly for a person with low vision.

Consideration should be given to the provision of interpreters where required and appropriate lighting where interpreters are working. Computer, electronics and presentation equipment should be flexible enough to cater for a presenter who may have a disability.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to and through the area.

Hearing augmentation to be provided where an inbuilt amplification system is installed (other than one used only for emergency warning) 

* in a room in a class 9b building; or  
* at any ticket office, teller’s booth, reception area or the like, where the public is screened from the service provider; or  
* in meeting rooms / auditoriums, conference rooms and any room used for judicatory purposes in a class 9b building;  
* available between 80 – 95% of the space dependant on the system type;  
* signage is to be provided to inform users of availability of system and location of receivers if required;  
* any screen associated with a Class 9b building and capable of displaying public announcements must be capable of supplementing any public address system, other than a public address systems used for emergency warning purposes only.

![Access Cartoons 053.tif][image6]

**Checklist**

| 15 | Meeting Spaces                           (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 15.1 | *Is there sufficient level circulation space provided for a person using a wheelchair to sit at a meeting table in various locations* |  |  |  |
| 15.2 | *Is there some seating available which is 450 – 520mm high with armrests provided at a height of 220 – 300mm above the seat and a back  **AS 1428.2 Cl. 27.2*** |  |  |  |
