# **16.0	Pathways (Accessways)**  {#16.0-pathways-(accessways)}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**AS / NZS 4586 \- 2013 		Slip resistance classification of new pedestrian surface materials** 

**Key Access Features**

A continuous accessible path of travel (CAPT) for people with disabilities begins at the car park and / or public transport set down area. This route can consist of pathways, roadways, ramps and the building entrance.

Key access features include a wide, level, firm, slip resistant surface in both wet and dry conditions, provision of any seating, bins, bollards, signs etc. located clear of the path of travel with an effective contrast, clear concise signage, adequate continual vertical clearance, tactile ground surface indicators at changes in direction, prior to ramps and kerb ramps, handrails on ramps, appropriate seating, colour contrasting edges and appropriate lighting for night time use.

If stairs are installed, an alternative accessible path of travel is required. Any stairs shall incorporate tactile ground surface indicators, handrails and contrasting stair nosings to Australian Standards.

**Requirements under the Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010 and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessway (CAPT) is required to be provided and maintained to the principal pedestrian entry of the building from:

* the allotment boundary;  
* any on-site car park on the allotment where a DAPB is required to be available;  
* any adjoining building required to be accessible that is connected by a pedestrian link.

An accessway (CAPT) is required to be provided and maintained:

* through the building to and through all areas required to be accessible.

**Checklist** 

| 16 | Pathways (Accessways)  CAPT      (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 16.1 | Does an accessible pathway lead users from the designated accessible parking bay to the building entrance **APS \- D3.2** |  |  |  |
| 16.2 | Does an accessible pathway lead users from the allotment boundary to the building entrance **APS \- D3.2** |  |  |  |
| 16.3 | Does an accessible pathway lead users from any adjoining building required to be accessible (if linked by a pedestrian pathway) **APS \- D3.2** |  |  |  |
| 16.4 | **If** there is an abutment of surfaces on the pathway, are they no greater than 3mm if the abutment is vertical, or 5mm if a bevelled edge **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.2** |  |  |  |
| 16.5 | **If** raked joint pavers are used, is the abutment of surfaces appropriate **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.2 Figure 7(A)** |  |  |  |
| 16.6 | *Do objects on the accessway, such as seats, tables, drinking fountains, bins etc have a luminance contrast  (intensity of light reflected) of not less than 0.3 (30%) to background or surrounding surfaces **AS 1428.2 Cl. 27.1 (b)*** |  |  |  |
| 16.7 | Are all accessways a min. width of 1000mm **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3.3** |   |  |  |

If linear opening is less than 8mm wide – Where linear openings are less than 8mm wide, orientation is optional.  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1** |  |  |  |
| 16.14 | *Are the edges of the pathways in colour contrast to their background (e.g. colour strip or grass on same ground surface)* |  |  |  |

| 16.16 | *Is there uniform appropriate lighting of the pathways for  night time use* |  |  |  |

# **17.0	Playgrounds** {#17.0-playgrounds}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**Relevant References:**

* **Everyone Can Play Guidelines**

**Key Access Features**

Playgrounds should incorporate a continuous accessible path of travel from car parking to the playground area, and to and through all play components and facilities. This should be traversable by a person using a wheelchair and incorporate tactile cues for people with low vision. A variety of accessible play equipment should be provided to create opportunities for children with a range of disabilities to participate, rather than just watch play activities.

Incorporation of a range of play components that provide opportunities for ground and above ground play, sound and movement as well as tactile experiences are important. Seating with backrests and armrests, accessible toilets should also be considered as well as access to shade, shelter and drinking water.

Clear concise signage is also important and clear lines of sight from any seating to and over the play equipment is recommended to assist safety of children.

![Access Cartoons 069.tif][image8]

**Checklist**

| 17 | Playgrounds                             (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 17.1 | *Is a designated accessible car parking provided in any onsite car park, close to the entry of the playground* |  |  |  |
| 17.2 | *Is there a continuous accessible path of travel, with a min. width of 1800mm to the playground from the property boundary and accessible car park* |  |  |  |
| 17.3 | *Is there a continuous accessible path of travel through the playground* |  |  |  |
| 17.4 | *Is there a firm, slip resistant pathway with a surface texture that is traversable by a person using a wheelchair to and through the playground equipment* |  |  |  |
| 17.5 | *Are appropriate directional and hazard TGSIs provided where required on the pathways* |  |  |  |
| 17.6 | *Are objects along the pathways set back a min. of 500mm, such as seats, tables, drinking fountains, bins etc. **AS1428.2*** |  |  |  |
| 17.7 | *Do objects along the pathways, such as seats, tables, drinking fountains, bins etc. have an effective contrast to surrounding surfaces*  |   |  |  |
| 17.8 | *Are the edges of the pathways in contrast to the background* |  |  |  |
| 17.9 | *Are there clear lines of sight available from seating / viewing areas to and over the play equipment* |  |  |  |
| 17.10 | *Is there appropriate shade / shelter over the play equipment*  |  |  |  |
| 17.11 | *Is there appropriate shade / shelter over the seating*  |  |  |  |
| 17.12 | *Is there a variety of accessible play components including ground level and above ground level components* |  |  |  |
| 17.13 | *Is there appropriate seating for children and adults with backrests and armrests* |  |  |  |
| 17.14 | *Are there accessible facilities e.g. drinking fountains, toilets, change tables*  |  |  |  |
| 17.15 | *Is there uniform appropriate lighting to the area* |  |  |  |
| 17.16 | *Is there clear, concise signage* |  |  |  |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **18.0	Ramps** {#18.0-ramps}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features:**

Ramps (or lifts) should be provided as an alternative to stairs, to ensure equity of access is provided for all building users. Ramps and landings shall incorporate appropriate widths, gradients, surfaces, handrails (both sides), tactile ground surface indicators (top and bottom), kerbs (both sides), vertical clearances, lighting, colour contrast edges and signage as required to Australian Standards.

Where a landing is provided at a doorway or with a change of direction, appropriate circulation space is required as detailed in Australian Standards. 

Depending on the location and the height of the rise several ramp types are available for use. These include threshold, step and kerb. 

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

All ramps (excluding fire isolated and ramps in areas not required to be accessible) are to:

* provide an appropriate gradient (max. 1:14), kerbs, handrails, landings, surfaces, TGSIs, width, vertical clearances;  
* be set back from any transverse pathway (external boundary min. 900mm / internal corridor min. 400mm) to eliminate any protrusion into that pathway;  
* a series of connected ramps must not have a combined vertical rise of more than 3.6m;  
* step ramps can be used where the rise is no greater than 190mm.  They require an appropriate grade, length and appropriate side splay (where cross traffic) or barrier  
* a landing for a step ramp must not overlap a landing for another step ramp or ramp (in high pedestrian traffic areas)

**Checklist**

| 18 | Ramps                                       (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 18.1 | **If** a vertical rise of more than 3.6m is provided through a series of connected ramps, is an alternative means of access provided **APS – D3.11** |  |  |  |
| 18.2 | Do all ramps have a slope / gradient where the max. ratio is 1:14 (tolerance 3% provide no section is steeper than 1:14)  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.3** |  |  |  |
| 18.3 | Do the 1:14 ramps have landings a min. of every nine metres or less at changes in directions **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.3** |  |  |  |
| 18.4 | **If** the ramp abuts an internal corridor, is it set back a min of 400mm or, if it abuts an external boundary a min. of 900mm  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.3** |  |  |  |
| 18.5 | **If** there are connected ramps / step ramps, are the landings free from any overlap **APS – D3.11 (b)** |  |  |  |
| 18.6 | *Do the edges of the ramps have colour contrast to their background **AS 1428.2 Cl. 8.4.5*** |  |  |  |
| 18.7 | *Is there appropriate uniform lighting of the ramp for night time use **AS 1428.2 Cl. 19*** |  |  |  |
| 18.8 | Are landings 1200mm (where no change of direction required) in length or greater ) (NOTE: sharp transitions are required between the planes of landings and ramps, refer AS for gradients) **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.8** |  |  |  |
| 18.9 | **If** the landing has a change of direction not exceeding 90°, is the landing a min. 1500mm, with the internal corner truncated for a min of 500mm in both directions **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.8** |  |  |  |
| 18.10 | **If** the landing has a 180° turn, is the landing a min. of 1540mm deep with other required dimensions as per the Standard **AS 1428.1 Cl. 7.8** |  |  |  |

# **19.0	Signage** {#19.0-signage}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**AS 1428.5 \- 2010		Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**Key Access Features**

Provision of appropriate signage that is clear, concise, easy to read and displays the blue international symbol of access, as appropriate, to assist people with intellectual and cognitive and sensory issues is important. Other considerations include Braille and tactile markings, audio announcements, location, height and lighting of signs. The international symbol of access and the international symbol of deafness shall be displayed where relevant and meet the minimum Australian Standards requirements for style, colour and layout.

Signage should be located at any set down area, car park or on directional pathways to buildings, at any non accessible entrance directing users to the nearest accessible entrance, as well as at and inside building entrances. It should also be provided inside buildings to indicate accessible facilities and direction to various facilities. Signage shall be appropriately illuminated and incorporate font styles and sizes such as San Serif \- Univers, Arial or Helvetica. A combination of upper and lower case lettering (Title Case) shall be used for ease of interpretation.

Text alternatives to audio signage should be available and appropriate signage including the international symbol of deafness, should be used to identify the location and type of assistive listening system that is installed in any room or area of the building.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

Signage (including Braille and tactile) is to be provided:

* at any non-accessible building entrance providing appropriate direction to an accessible entrance;  
* at accessible toilets (including information about the facility configuration i.e. LH or RH);   
* at any non accessible bank of toilets directing a person to the accessible bank of toilets;  
* at ambulant toilet facilities;  
* at spaces incorporating hearing augmentation (including information about type of system in use and availability / location of receivers).

Braille and tactile signs must be illuminated (as required) to ensure luminance contrast requirements are met at all times during which the sign is required to be read.

Note: The BCA has additional requirements in relation to signage (egress).

![Access Cartoons 006.tif][image9]

**Checklist**

| 19 | Signage                                          (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 19.1 | Is appropriate signage available where directional decisions are made **APS – DP1 (b) / AS 1428.1 CL 5.1** |  |  |  |
| 19.2 | *Is signage (including tactile and Braille) located at the main building entry, both inside and out, giving directional and general information about buildings and facilities including services and access for people with disabilities* |  |  |  |
| 19.3 | **If** there is a non accessible entrance doorway, is there appropriate signage provided directing users to accessible entrance **APS – D3.6 (e) / D4 / AS 1428.1 Cl. 5.1** |  |  |  |
| 19.4 | Where the symbol for access is used, does it comply with the international standard in style, colour and layout  **APS – D3.6 / D4 / AS 1428.1 Cl. 5.2** |  |  |  |
| 19.5 | Does signage, including the international symbol of deafness, indicate the area where an assistive listening system is operational and the area covered **APS – D3.6 (b) (i) / D4 / D3.7 (1) (2) (3) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 5.2** |  |  |  |
| 19.6 | Does signage including the international symbol of deafness, indicate which type of system is in place **APS – D3.6 (b) (ii) / D4 / D3.7 (1) (2) (3) / AS 1428.1 Cl. 5.2** |  |  |  |
| 19.7 | **If** receivers are being used for hearing augmentation, does the signage indicate where the receivers can be obtained **APS D3.6 (b) (iii)** |  |  |  |
| 19.8 | Is raised tactile information provided on signs between 1200 – 1600mm **APS – D3.6 (b) / D4 / AS 1428.1 CL 5.1** |  |  |  |
| 19.9 | Is there appropriate illumination of signage for day and night use (where required e.g. to maintain luminance) **APS – D4.5** |  |  |  |
| 19.10 | **If** there is a non-accessible toilet provided, is there signage available that directs users to an accessible toilet (where in different locations) **APS – D3.6 (f) / D4** |  |  |  |
| 19.11 | Does the signage indicate if the accessible toilet facility is suitable for left or right hand **APS – D3.6 (c) / D4 / AS 1428.1 Cl 5.1** |  |  |  |
| 19.12 | **If** available on the sign, is the text provided in **Title Case APS – D4.3 (2); Title Case AS 1428.1 C 5.1**  |  |  |  |
| 19.13 | Is there signage (incorporating raised text and Braille, and raised and visual symbols) installed identifying available sanitary facilities **APS-D3.6 (a) / AS 1428.1 Cl 5.1** |  |  |  |

| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |

Mandatory requirement*, preferred requirement*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **20.0	Stairs** {#20.0-stairs}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features**

Any steps or stairs shall be easily identifiable by contrast on stair nosings. They shall incorporate enclosed risers with slip resistant surfaces as well as appropriate handrails on both sides. These shall extend past the top and bottom step on both sides of the stairs.

Other key access features include tactile ground surface indicators at the top and bottom of stairs and at landings as required, and appropriate lighting for night time use.

An accessible alternative to stairs should also be provided. e.g. ramp or lift.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

All stairs (excluding fire isolated and stairs in areas not required to be accessible) are to:

* provide appropriate landings, nosings, handrails, TGSIs, width, vertical clearances;   
* be set back from any transverse pathway (external boundary min. 900mm / internal corridor min. one tread width plus 300mm) to eliminate any protrusion into that pathway;   
* nosings are required on fire isolated stairs. 

**NOTE: 	Under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010*, an alternative means of access (e.g. ramp or lift) may not be required to the upper level of some small buildings. Refer to APS for further detail.**

**Checklist** 

| 20 | Stairs                                           (tick relevant box) | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 20.1 | Is there an accessible alternative route close to the stairs (e.g. ramp, lift) (where required – see Concessions in Premises Standards) **APS – 3.3 (f) 4.4 / D3.1 / D3.2 / D3.3 / E3.6** |  |  |  |
| 20.2 | **If** the stairs abut an internal corridor / external boundary, are they setback to allow a min. of one tread width plus 300mm internally / min. 900mm externally **AS 1428.1 Cl. 8.1 (a) (b) / 9** |  |  |  |

# **21.0	Swimming Pools** {#21.0-swimming-pools}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features**

Accessible car parking as close as possible to the facility entrance is important. A continuous accessible path of travel incorporating a slip resistant surface shall be provided to and through the facility and direct, level access to any pools should be available.

Key access features include beach entry, ramped or platform lift access to pools (with aquatic wheelchairs provided). Hoists should be installed in addition to these features.  Other important features include, handrails at pool entry points, stair nosings with effective contrasts and tactile ground surface indicators to Australian Standards, to all stairs / steps / ramps. Clear identification of any ramped, beach entry, platform lift or stepped access within a pool is also important.  
   
Appropriate signage to warn users if the pool facility has a water movement sequence (i.e. waves) and an audible and visual alarm to facilities with a water movement sequence, to inform users that this activity is to commence should be provided, particularly to support users who are Deaf or hard of hearing and users with low vision.

Consideration should also be given to provision of appropriate seating, which allows integrated wheelchair spaces and access at various locations and an accessible unisex shower / change area (preferably with toilet included).

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

**NOTE:	Under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010*, a pool that has a perimeter \<40m is not required to have some alternative means of access available (e.g. ramp / zero grade). A variety of entry means are permitted for pools with a perimeter up to 70m. Pools with a perimeter \>70m are not permitted to have sling entry only. Refer to APS and info below for further detail.** 

Pools (size dependant) require an accessible entry / exit by means of (type dependant on size of pool):

* a fixed or movable ramp and aquatic wheelchair;  
* zero depth entry (max. 1:14 grade) and aquatic wheelchair;  
* platform swimming pool lift and aquatic wheelchair; or  
* a sling style pool lift.

![Access Cartoons 059.tif][image10]

**Checklist**

| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 21.1 | Is there a CAPT to the poolside  **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3**  |  |  |  |
| 21.2 | Are there slip resistant floor surfaces surrounding the pool **AS 1428.1 Cl. 4.1**  |  |  |  |
| 21.3 | Where required, is there an alternative means of entry e.g.  fixed or movable ramp and aquatic wheelchair zero depth entry at grade of 1:14 and an aquatic wheelchair  platform swimming pool lift and an aquatic wheelchair  sling style swimming pool lift (**not permitted as only means of access into pools with perimeter \>70m)** **APS – D3.10 / D5** |  |  |  |
| 21.4 | Is there a CAPT to any spa or sauna **AS 1428.1 Cl. 3** |  |  |  |
| 21.5 | *Are there appropriate handrails (30 – 52mm dia. at 900 – 1100mm high) available on both sides of the entry point* |  |  |  |
| 21.6 | *Are there any rails around the perimeter of the pool for use when in the water (e.g. hydrotherapy pool)* |  |  |  |
| 21.7 | *Is there a Unisex accessible change room available* |  |  |  |

# **22.0	Spectator Facilities** {#22.0-spectator-facilities}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2021	Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work**   
**AS 1428.2 \- 1992	Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**  
**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**  
**AS 1428.5 – 2010	Communication for people who are deaf or hearing impaired**

**Key Access Features**

Consideration shall be given to provision of appropriate seating, which allows integrated wheelchair spaces and access at various locations as well as sufficient space for people using wheelchairs to sit with friends, partners etc. in the standard spectator area.

Other key access features include clear lines of sight for viewing, suitable scoring systems for people with low vision , people who are Deaf or hard of hearing and proximity to emergency exits. Handrails, stair nosings and tactile ground surface indicators to all stairs, steps and ramps to Australian Standards is important.

Provision of accessible toilets, (unisex preferred) where any toilets are provided is necessary.

Provision for storing wheelchairs and walking aids in a safe, accessible area convenient to the user activity is also important to ensure safety of all users.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

Where fixed seating is provided in a Class 9b building, wheelchair accessible spaces are required in a variety of locations, dependent on the number of fixed seats. Removable seats may be used.  

In a cinema, specific requirements regarding the number of seats and their location must be addressed.

| Number of fixed seats in a room or space  | Number of wheelchair seating spaces | Grouping and location |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Up to 150 | 3 spaces | 1 single space; and 1 group of 2 spaces |
| 151 to 800 | 3 spaces plus  1 additional space for each additional 50 seats or part thereof in excess of 150 seats | Not less than 1 single space; and Not less than 1 group of 2 spaces; and  not more than 5 spaces in any other group  |
| 801 to 10 000 | 16 spaces plus 1 additional space for each additional 100 seats or part thereof in excess of 800 seats | Not less than 2 single spaces; and Not less than 2 groups of 2 spaces; and Not more than 5 spaces in any other group; and the location of spaces is to be representative of the range of seating provided |
| More than  10 000 | 108 spaces plus 1 additional space for each additional 200 seats or part thereof in excess of 10 000 seats | Not less than 5 single spaces; and not less than 5 groups of 2 spaces; and not more than 10 spaces in any other group; and the location of spaces is to be representative of the range of seating provided |

**Source – *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010***

**Checklist**

# **23.0	Tactile Ground Surface Indicators** {#23.0-tactile-ground-surface-indicators}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1428.4.1 \- 2009	Design for access and mobility – Tactile Indicators**

**Key Access Features**

Tactile Ground Surface Indicators (TGSIs) are specific tiles or materials with raised projections installed on the ground or floor surface to provide tactile information which can assist a person with low vision in orientation and way finding. 

Two types of TGSIs are currently used in Australia.

**Warning Indicators**: (raised domes) are used at intersections, mid block pedestrian crossings, other pedestrian / vehicle conflict areas and bus stops. They are also used where other hazards are present such as wharves or jetties, platform edges or prior to barriers on pathways such as signs or other obstructions, including overhead obstructions. They also inform people about changes in the direction of path of travel. 

**Directional Indicators:** (raised longitudinal strips) These assist people to negotiate difficult environments such as open or busy spaces, or to locate specific objects or locations such as bus stops, train platforms and other installations.

Directional and warning TGSIs are used on footpaths at intersections and mid block pedestrian crossings.

These should be installed so that people with low vision are able to locate the directional indicators leading towards the crossing point. There should be warning indicators prior to reaching the road surface at the kerb ramp or crossing point, including medians.

Directional and warning indicators are also used at bus stops for orientating pedestrians, including people who are blind or have low vision. Domed warning TGSIs are used to indicate the presence of any hazard, kerb edge or change of direction. 

Warning TGSIs are used in other areas where a hazard may be present. e.g. at pedestrian / vehicle conflicts where a driver may not be able to see pedestrians walking along a footpath or close to the edge of a jetty, wharf or train platform to alert a person with low vision to imminent danger. They may also be used at other locations where there may be an obstruction within a pathway such as a sign or other barrier.

Many people with low vision still retain some vision, so it is important that TGSIs are readily distinguishable by luminance contrast (can be achieved by tonal contrast within the same colour) and from adjacent surfaces. 

The consistent use and placement of TGSIs is a key consideration during installation, however TGSIs should not be overused. They are required when there are insufficient alternative or ‘natural’ tactile cues to warn of a hazard or change of direction.

TGSIs should also be installed where possible, so as to reduce interference with the manoeuvrability of wheelchairs or use of the area by other people with disabilities, including pedestrians with ambulatory disabilities.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

Tactile Ground Surface Indicators are to be provided to warn a person with low vision that they are approaching:

* stairways (excluding fire isolated stairways);  
* an escalator;  
* a passenger conveyor or moving walk;  
* a ramp (excluding fire isolated ramps);  
* an overhead obstruction less than 2m (in the absence of a suitable barrier) (other than a doorway);  
* level transitions between a vehicular way adjacent to a pedestrian entrance to a building.

Luminance contrasts are required to meet Australian Standards:

* where Tactile Ground Surface Indicators (TGSIs) are installed – this varies from 30% to 60% dependant on the installation type.

**Checklist**

# **24.0a and b	Toilets (Designated Accessible Toilets)** {#24.0a-and-b-toilets-(designated-accessible-toilets)}

**Relevant Australian Standards:**

**AS 1428.1 – 2001		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.1 – 2021		Design for access and mobility – General requirements for access – New building work** 

**AS 1428.2 \- 1992		Design for access and mobility \- Enhanced and additional requirements – Buildings and facilities**

**AS / NZS 1680.0 – 2009	Interior lighting – Safe movement**

**AS / NZS 1680.1 – 2006 	Interior lighting – General principles and recommendations**

**Key Access Features**

Where sanitary facilities are provided accessible toilets and showers should also be provided. Unisex facilities are required as a male user may have a female carer or vice a versa. 

Signage including the international symbol of access as well as the term ‘Accessible Toilet’ is preferred to ‘Disabled Toilet’, as this indicates the facility is for use by anyone, including families. 

Baby change tables should only be installed in the toilet, if they do not encroach on the required circulation space for an accessible toilet, when left in the open or closed position. Some users with disabilities may not be able to place the change table back on the wall or move it out of the required circulation space when it is left open.

Compliance with relevant Australian Standards is crucial in accessible toilets, as many people with disabilities will not be able to use the facilities unless they are installed to minimum Standards. The most important consideration is the size of the area and the location of fittings to ensure that a person can easily move around and use the toilet and hand basin once inside. These Standards should be referred to prior to undertaking any works.

The BCA does not allow for provision of combined male/female ambulant toilets. The BCA requires separate male ambulant and separate female ambulant toilets.

**Note**: Toilets (2001 and 2021\)

Prior to the introduction of the Commonwealth *Disability (Access to Premises- Buildings Standards) 2010* (DAPS) the key reference for the dimensions of unisex accessible toilets (USAT), was Australian Standard 1428.1: 2001\. With the introduction of the Premises Standards and updates to referenced Australian Standards, AS 1428.1 2021 is now the primary reference for USATs.

However, the Premises Standards includes a concession for USATs in existing buildings, granted a building permit prior to 1st May 2011\. In practical terms, this concession means that if a USAT is part of a New Part in a building upgrade and the USAT meets the requirements of AS1428. 2001 they are not required to be upgraded to meet the requirements of AS 1428.1 2021\.

If however, the existing USAT does not meet the requirements of AS 1428.1 2001 then the USAT would need to be upgraded to meet the requirements of AS 1428.1 2021\.

**Requirements under the *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010* and referenced Australian Standards**

An accessible unisex sanitary compartment is required 

| Class of Building | Minimum accessible unisex sanitary compartments to be provided |
| :---- | :---- |
| Class 1b | not less than 1: and where private accessible unisex sanitary compartments are provided for an accessible bedroom, common accessible unisex sanitary compartments need not be provided |
| Class 2 | Where sanitary compartments are provided in common areas, not less than 1 |
| Class 3 and Class 9c aged care building | in every accessible sole-occupancy unit provided with sanitary compartments within the accessible sole-occupancy unit, not less than 1: and at each bank of sanitary compartments containing male and female sanitary compartments provided in common areas, not less than 1 |
| Class 5, 6, 7, 8 and 9 – except for within a ward area of a Class 9a health care building | Where clause F2.3 of the BCA requires closet pans: 1 on every storey containing sanitary compartments; and Where a storey has more than 1 bank of sanitary compartments containing male and female sanitary compartments at not less than 50% of those banks |
| Class 10a – except A Class 10a appurtenant to another Class of building; and A sanitary compartment dedicated to a single caravan / camping site | At each bank of sanitary compartments containing male and female sanitary compartments, not less than 1 |

**Source – *Disability (Access to Premises – Buildings) Standards 2010***  
At each bank of toilets where there is one or more toilets in addition to a unisex accessible toilet, an ambulant toilet is to be provided. 

A unisex accessible toilet must not be located so that it can be entered without crossing an area reserved for one sex only.

A pan circulation space (min. 1900mm x 2300mm x 2000mm high) is required, with allowance for the appropriate fixtures and fittings to be provided within this space.

The requirement that an accessible sanitary compartment have the abovementioned pan circulation space does not apply to:

1) existing accessible sanitary compartments;   
2) existing sanitary compartments suitable for use by a person with a disability.

For the above section (a) or (b) to apply the accessible sanitary compartment must:

* comply with AS 1428.1—2001, *Design for access and mobility, Part 1: General requirements for access—New building work*; and   
* be located in either a new part, or an affected part, of a building*.*

**Actions:** advocate, consider, construct, ensure, install, maintain, modify, mark, provide, realign, reconfigure, reconstruct, redesign, relocate, remark, remove, repair, replace, trim, upgrade, widen.

# **25.0	Accessible Adult Change Facilities** {#25.0-accessible-adult-change-facilities}

**Relevant Legislation:**

**Disability (Access to Premises- Buildings) Standards 2010**

**National Construction Code 2022**

**Key Access Features**

An accessible adult change facility is intended to be used by people who cannot use standard accessible toilets. This may include people with an acquired brain injury, cerebral palsy, multiple sclerosis, spina bifida, motor neurone disease and their carers, as well as many other people with a disability.

People need a toilet that contains an adult size adjustable changing table, a ceiling hoist, enough space (horizontally and vertically) and a safe and clean environment. Without these items, an accessible toilet that meets the Australian Standards for Access and Mobility is not functional. 

The Premises Standards requires Accessible Adult Change Facilities (AACF) to be installed in larger shopping centres and aquatic facilities, major sporting and recreational complexes, cultural facilities, and larger airports.  Although not formally required, accessible adult change facilities are also being installed in other venues such as premier train stations, hospitals, highway facilities, civic centres and other locations where operators such as councils believe they will be of benefit.

AACF also underpin the following National Disability Insurance Scheme (NDIS) policy directions:

* Increased participation of people with disability, their families and carers in the social, cultural, recreational and sporting life of the community;  
* Improved accessibility of the built and natural environment through planning and regulatory systems, maximising the participation and inclusion of every member of the community;  
* A public, private and community transport system that is accessible for the whole community.

An AACF also enhances the carer’s physical wellbeing through removing the need to lift the person with a disability and through increased social opportunities and the removal of the everyday stress of planning around the bathroom needs of the person they are caring for.

An AACF is designed to accommodate two carers and a person (who may be using a wheelchair) who needs assistance to attend to their personal hygiene and toileting needs.

The ceiling hoist is designed to provide coverage of the whole room in order to facilitate ease of access to the toilet and to the change table.  The toilet pan must be of the “peninsula” type with movable handrails either side of the toilet bowl to allow a carer on each side to assist. Further requirements, such as those for door controls and signage, the need for a full round seat, secure fixings, load ratings, luminance contrast, flushing controls, and for the backrest and grabrails, aim in their entirety to address the range of disability and access challenges.  

Provision of two parallel changing rails, each at differing heights, are installed to provide a user with support when they are having their clothing adjusted.  Other requirements such as adjustable hot water at the basin \- controlled via a lever tap or sensor controls \- provision of a mirror and shelf, soap dispenser and clothes hook, and the need for operational instructions for the hoist and change table, also enhance the usability of the facility.

**Requirements as per the Premises Standards**

**F2.9 Accessible adult change facilities**

(1) *Accessible* adult change facilities required by subclause (2):  
(a) must be constructed in accordance with Part F3; and  
(b) cannot be combined with another *sanitary compartment*.

2\) One unisex *accessible* adult change facility must be provided in an *accessible* part of a:  
(a) Class 6 building that is a shopping centre having a design occupancy of not less than 3,500 people, calculated on the basis of the *floor area* and containing a minimum of 2 *sole-occupancy units*; and  
(b) Class 9b sports venue or the like that:  
(i) has a design occupancy of not less than 35,000 spectators; or  
(ii) contains a *swimming pool* that has a perimeter of not less than 70 m and  
that is *required* by Table D3.1 to be *accessible*; and  
(c) museum, art gallery or the like having a design occupancy of not less than 1,500 patrons; and  
(d) theatre or the like having a design occupancy of not less than 1,500 patrons; and  
(e) passenger use area of an airport terminal building within an airport that accepts domestic and/or international flights that are public transport services as defined in the *Transport Standards*.

(3) For the purposes of subclause (2), design occupancy must be calculated in  
accordance with clause D1.13 of the *BCA*, but excluding any area that:

(a) can only be accessed by staff, employees, contractors, maintenance personnel and the like; or  
(b) is subject to an exemption under clause D3.4.

| 25.79 | **Door and door controls**  Are the entrance door and associated door controls automated |  |  |  |
| 25.80 | Does the threshold incorporate a smooth transition without a step or lip |  |  |  |
| 25.81 | Is the minimum clear opening width 1100mm in locations where beach wheelchairs are likely to be used |  |  |  |
| 25.82 | Is the minimum clear opening width 950mm in all other locations |  |  |  |

| 25.0 | Accessible adult change facilities         (tick relevant box)  | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 25.83 | Does the doorway achieve a luminance contrast of at least 30% between the following components (circle as appropriate) : Door leaf and door jamb; or  (ii) Door leaf and adjacent wall; or iii) Architraves (where used) and adjacent wall; or  (iv) Door leaf and architrave (where used); or (v) Door jamb and adjacent wall.  |  |  |  |
| 25.84 | Does the door have a gentle opening and closing movement |  |  |  |
| 25.85 | Does the door have sufficient dwell time |  |  |  |
| 25.86 | Does the door have a fail-safe opening mechanism that opens the door if an obstruction is detected during its closing movement |  |  |  |
| 25.87 | Are door controls located internally and externally between 900mm and 1200mm above finished floor level |  |  |  |
| 25.88 | Are door controls located internally and externally not less than 500mm from any internal corner |  |  |  |
| 25.89 | Do door control buttons have a minimum diameter of 25mm |  |  |  |
| 25.90 | Do door control buttons sit proud of the surrounding surface  |  |  |  |
| 25.91 | Do door control buttons activate the operation before the button becomes level with the adjacent surface |  |  |  |
| 25.92 | Are door control buttons of a contrasting colour to the surrounding plate |  |  |  |
| 25.93 | Do door controls include the words “Push to Open” on the surrounding plates of both internal and external door controls |  |  |  |
| 25.94 | Do door controls provide the following indicator lights: “Occupied” and “Vacant” on the external plate |  |  |  |
| 25.95 | Do door controls provide the following indicator lights: “Locked” and “Unlocked” on the internal plate |  |  |  |
| 25.96 | Is Braille and tactile signage complying with BCA available to identify the door controls |  |  |  |
| 25.97 | Does external signage incorporate the symbol as shown in BCA |  |  |  |
| 25.98 | Does the external signage incorporate the words “Accessible Adult Change Facility” |  |  |  |
| 25.99 | Is the symbol required by Q \*\*\* above, provided with a blue background (B21, Ultramarine) with the hoist and table elements shown in white.  |  |  |  |

| 25.0 | Accessible adult change facilities         (tick relevant box)  | Y | N | Action |
| :---: | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 25.100 | Does the signage incorporate Braille and tactile which meets the requirements of BCA |  |  |  |
| 25.101 | Is signage provided within the facility which includes the following information for the hoist **and** change table (circle as appropriate)  Operating instructions Safe working load limits  |  |  |  |
